Problem Statement\n\nSymphony is a long-running automation service that continuously reads work from an issue tracker\n(Linear in this specification version), creates an isolated workspace for each issue, and runs a\ncoding agent session for that issue inside the workspace.\n\nThe service solves four operational problems:\n\n- It turns issue execution into a repeatable daemon workflow instead of manual scripts.\n- It isolates agent execution in per-issue workspaces so agent commands run only inside per-issue\n  workspace directories.\n- It keeps the workflow policy in-repo (`WORKFLOW.md`) so teams version the agent prompt and runtime\n  settings with their code.\n- It provides enough observability to operate and debug multiple concurrent agent runs.\n\nImplementations are expected to document their trust and safety posture explicitly. This\nspecification does not require a single approval, sandbox, or operator-confirmation policy; some\nimplementations may target trusted environments with a high-trust configuration, while others may\nrequire stricter approvals or sandboxing.\n\nImportant boundary:\n\n- Symphony is a scheduler/runner and tracker reader.\n- Ticket writes (state transitions, comments, PR links) are typically performed by the coding agent\n  using tools available in the workflow/runtime environment.\n- A successful run may end at a workflow-defined handoff state (for example `Human Review`), not\n  necessarily `Done`.\n\n## 2. Goals and Non-Goals\n\n### 2.1 Goals\n\n- Poll the issue tracker on a fixed cadence and dispatch work with bounded concurrency.\n- Maintain a single authoritative orchestrator state for dispatch, retries, and reconciliation.\n- Create deterministic per-issue workspaces and preserve them across runs.\n- Stop active runs when issue state changes make them ineligible.\n...\n</persisted-output>","is_error":false}]},"uuid":"045dfe8e-ac4c-46da-ac6b-9bc1a5ba71eb","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:19:04.351Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"ebbcc65b-d9f2-4605-9fd3-cddfc5617aab","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

This value can communicate context\n    or request input required to resume execution.\n\n    In a given node, the first invocation of this function raises a `GraphInterrupt`\n    exception, halting execution. The provided `value` is included with the exception\n    and sent to the client executing the graph.\n\n    A client resuming the graph must use the [`Command`][langgraph.types.Command]\n    primitive to specify a value for the interrupt and continue execution.\n    The graph resumes from the start of the node, **re-executing** all logic.\n\n    If a node contains multiple `interrupt` calls, LangGraph matches resume values\n    to interrupts based on their order in the node. This list of resume values\n    is scoped to the specific task executing the node and is not shared across tasks.\n\n    To use an `interrupt`, you must enable a checkpointer, as the feature relies\n    on persisting the graph state.\n\n    !!! example\n\n        ```python\n        import uuid\n        from typing import Optional\n        from typing_extensions import TypedDict\n\n        from langgraph.checkpoint.memory import InMemorySaver\n        from langgraph.constants import START\n        from langgraph.graph import StateGraph\n        from langgraph.types import interrupt, Command\n\n\n        class State(TypedDict):\n            \\\"\\\"\\\"The graph state.\\\"\\\"\\\"\n\n            foo: str\n            human_value: Optional[str]\n            \\\"\\\"\\\"Human value will be updated using an interrupt.\\\"\\\"\\\"\n\n\n        def node(state: State):\n            answer = interrupt(\n                # This value will be sent to the client\n                # as part of the interrupt information.\n                \\\"what is your age?\\\"\n            )\n            print(f\\\"> Received an input from the interrupt: {answer}\\\")\n            return {\\\"human_value\\\": answer}\n\n\n        builder = StateGraph(State)\n        builder.add_node(\\\"node\\\", node)\n        builder.add_edge(START, \\\"node\\\")\n\n        # A checkpointer must be enabled for interrupts to work!\n        checkpointer = InMemorySaver()\n        graph = builder.compile(checkpointer=checkpointer)\n\n        config = {\n            \\\"configurable\\\": {\n                \\\"thread_id\\\": uuid.uuid4(),\n            }\n        }\n\n        for chunk in graph.stream({\\\"foo\\\": \\\"abc\\\"}, config):\n            print(chunk)\n\n        # > Received an input from the interrupt: some input from a human!!!\n        # > {'node': {'human_value': 'some input from a human!!!'}}\n        ```\n\n    Args:\n        value: The value to surface to the client when the graph is interrupted.\n\n    Returns:\n        Any: On subsequent invocations within the same node (same task to be precise), returns the value provided during the first invocation\n\n    Raises:\n        GraphInterrupt: On the first invocation within the node, halts execution and surfaces the provided value to the client.\n    \"\"\"\n    from langgraph._internal._constants import (\n        CONFIG_KEY_CHECKPOINT_NS,\n        CONFIG_KEY_SCRATCHPAD,\n        CONFIG_KEY_SEND,\n        RESUME,\n    )\n    from langgraph.config import get_config\n    from langgraph.errors import GraphInterrupt\n\n    conf = get_config()[\"configurable\"]\n    # find current resume value\n    v = scratchpad.get_null_resume(True)\n    if v is not None:\n        assert len(scratchpad.resume) == idx, (scratchpad.resume, idx)\n        scratchpad.resume.append(v)\n        conf[CONFIG_KEY_SEND]([(RESUME, scratchpad.resume)])\n        return v\n    # Normal update: uses the reducer (operator.add)\n            return {\"messages\": [\"a\"]}\n\n        def node_b(state: State):\n            # Overwrite: bypasses the reducer and replaces the entire value\n            return {\"messages\": Overwrite(value=[\"b\"])}\n\n        builder = StateGraph(State)\n        builder.add_node(\"node_a\", node_a)\n        builder.add_node(\"node_b\", node_b)\n        builder.set_entry_point(\"node_a\")\n        builder.add_edge(\"node_a\", \"node_b\")\n        graph = builder.compile()\n\n        # This\n   172Ôćĺ            is inclusive of all retries.\n   173Ôćĺ        schedule_to_start_timeout: Max amount of time the activity can take to\n   174Ôćĺ            be started from first being scheduled.\n   175Ôćĺ        start_to_close_timeout: Max amount of time a single activity run can\n   176Ôćĺ            take from when it starts to when it completes. This is per retry.\n   177Ôćĺ        heartbeat_timeout: How frequently an activity must invoke heartbeat\n   178Ôćĺ            while running before it is considered timed out.\n   179Ôćĺ        retry_policy: How an activity is retried on failure. If unset, a\n   180Ôćĺ--\n   181Ôćĺasync def execute_activity(\n   182Ôćĺ    activity: CallableAsyncNoParam[ReturnType],\n   183Ôćĺ    *,\n   184Ôćĺ    task_queue: str | None = None,\n   185Ôćĺ    schedule_to_close_timeout: timedelta | None = None,\n   186Ôćĺ    schedule_to_start_timeout: timedelta | None = None,\n   187Ôćĺ    start_to_close_timeout: timedelta | None = None,\n   188Ôćĺ    heartbeat_timeout: timedelta | None = None,\n   189Ôćĺ    retry_policy: temporalio.common.RetryPolicy | None = None,\n   190Ôćĺ    cancellation_type: ActivityCancellationType = ActivityCancellationType.TRY_CANCEL,\n   191Ôćĺ    activity_id: str | None = None,\n   192Ôćĺ    versioning_intent: VersioningIntent | None = None,\n   193Ôćĺ    summary: str | None = None,\n   194Ôćĺ    priority: temporalio.common.Priority = temporalio.common.Priority.default,\n   195Ôćĺ) -> ReturnType: ...\n   196Ôćĺ\n   197Ôćĺ\n   198Ôćĺ# Overload for sync no-param activity\n   199Ôćĺ@overload\n   200Ôćĺasync def execute_activity("}]},"uuid":"2e0d1811-283a-4608-9d5a-c33c4565bc63","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:19:41.751Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"3e8a1cb0-0898-469b-8efb-6c76a7073292","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"48cd13f0-7d91-48f5-8ab4-62e6b1126929","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4cff8217-4055-4c23-8140-7e344f8eaa3c","agentId":"a357586bccfafb0e5","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01BKigu3pxhhYgvnPj84ice3","type":"tool_result","content":"     1Ôćĺ# Symphony Service Specification\n     2Ôćĺ\n     3ÔćĺStatus: Draft v1 (language-agnostic)\n     4Ôćĺ\n     5ÔćĺPurpose: Define a service that orchestrates coding agents to get project work done.\n     6Ôćĺ\n     7Ôćĺ## 1. Problem Statement\n     8Ôćĺ\n     9ÔćĺSymphony is a long-running automation service that continuously reads work from an issue tracker\n    10Ôćĺ(Linear in this specification version), creates an isolated workspace for each issue, and runs a\n    11Ôćĺcoding agent session for that issue inside the workspace.\n    12Ôćĺ\n    13ÔćĺThe service solves four operational problems:\n    14Ôćĺ\n    15Ôćĺ- It turns issue execution into a repeatable daemon workflow instead of manual scripts.\n    16Ôćĺ- It isolates agent execution in per-issue workspaces so agent commands run only inside per-issue\n    17Ôćĺ  workspace directories.\n    18Ôćĺ- It keeps the workflow policy in-repo (`WORKFLOW.md`) so teams version the agent prompt and runtime\n    19Ôćĺ  settings with their code.\n    20Ôćĺ- It provides enough observability to operate and debug multiple concurrent agent runs.\n    21Ôćĺ\n    22ÔćĺImplementations are expected to document their trust and safety posture explicitly. This\n    23Ôćĺspecification does not require a single approval, sandbox, or operator-confirmation policy; some\n    24Ôćĺimplementations may target trusted environments with a high-trust configuration, while others may\n    25Ôćĺrequire stricter approvals or sandboxing.\n    26Ôćĺ\n    27ÔćĺImportant boundary:\n    28Ôćĺ\n    29Ôćĺ- Symphony is a scheduler/runner and tracker reader.\n    30Ôćĺ- Ticket writes (state transitions, comments, PR links) are typically performed by the coding agent\n    31Ôćĺ  using tools available in the workflow/runtime environment.\n    32Ôćĺ- A successful run may end at a workflow-defined handoff state (for example `Human Review`), not\n    33Ôćĺ  necessarily `Done`.\n    34Ôćĺ\n    35Ôćĺ## 2. Goals and Non-Goals\n    36Ôćĺ\n    37Ôćĺ### 2.1 Goals\n    38Ôćĺ\n    39Ôćĺ- Poll the issue tracker on a fixed cadence and dispatch work with bounded concurrency.\n    40Ôćĺ- Maintain a single authoritative orchestrator state for dispatch, retries, and reconciliation.\n    41Ôćĺ- Create deterministic per-issue workspaces and preserve them across runs.\n    42Ôćĺ- Stop active runs when issue state changes make them ineligible.\n    43Ôćĺ- Recover from transient failures with exponential backoff.\n    44Ôćĺ- Load runtime behavior from a repository-owned `WORKFLOW.md` contract.\n    45Ôćĺ- Expose operator-visible observability (at minimum structured logs).\n    46Ôćĺ- Support restart recovery without requiring a persistent database.\n    47Ôćĺ\n    48Ôćĺ### 2.2 Non-Goals\n    49Ôćĺ\n    50Ôćĺ- Rich web UI or multi-tenant control plane.\n    51Ôćĺ- Prescribing a specific dashboard or terminal UI implementation.\n    52Ôćĺ- General-purpose workflow engine or distributed job scheduler.\n    53Ôćĺ- Built-in business logic for how to edit tickets, PRs, or comments. (That logic lives in the\n    54Ôćĺ  workflow prompt and agent tooling.)\n    55Ôćĺ- Mandating strong sandbox controls beyond what the coding agent and host OS provide.\n    56Ôćĺ- Mandating a single default approval, sandbox, or operator-confirmation posture for all\n    57Ôćĺ  implementations.\n    58Ôćĺ\n    59Ôćĺ## 3. System Overview\n    60Ôćĺ\n    61Ôćĺ### 3.1 Main Components\n    62Ôćĺ\n    63Ôćĺ1. `Workflow Loader`\n    64Ôćĺ   - Reads `WORKFLOW.md`.\n    65Ôćĺ   - Parses YAML front matter and prompt body.\n    66Ôćĺ   - Returns `{config, prompt_template}`.\n    67Ôćĺ\n    68Ôćĺ2. `Config Layer`\n    69Ôćĺ   - Exposes typed getters for workflow config values.\n    70Ôćĺ   - Applies defaults and environment variable indirection.\n    71Ôćĺ   - Performs validation used by the orchestrator before dispatch.\n    72Ôćĺ\n    73Ôćĺ3. `Issue Tracker Client`\n    74Ôćĺ   - Fetches candidate issues in active states.\n    75Ôćĺ   - Fetches current states for specific issue IDs (reconciliation).\n    76Ôćĺ   - Fetches terminal-state issues during startup cleanup.\n    77Ôćĺ   - Normalizes tracker payloads into a stable issue model.\n    78Ôćĺ\n    79Ôćĺ4. `Orchestrator`\n    80Ôćĺ   - Owns the poll tick.\n    81Ôćĺ   - Owns the in-memory runtime state.\n    82Ôćĺ   - Decides which issues to dispatch, retry, stop, or release.\n    83Ôćĺ   - Tracks session metrics and retry queue state.\n    84Ôćĺ\n    85Ôćĺ5. `Workspace Manager`\n    86Ôćĺ   - Maps issue identifiers to workspace paths.\n    87Ôćĺ   - Ensures per-issue workspace directories exist.\n    88Ôćĺ   - Runs workspace lifecycle hooks.\n    89Ôćĺ   - Cleans workspaces for terminal issues.\n    90Ôćĺ\n    91Ôćĺ6. `Agent Runner`\n    92Ôćĺ   - Creates workspace.\n    93Ôćĺ   - Builds prompt from issue + workflow template.\n    94Ôćĺ   - Launches the coding agent app-server client.\n    95Ôćĺ   - Streams agent updates back to the orchestrator.\n    96Ôćĺ\n    97Ôćĺ7. `Status Surface` (optional)\n    98Ôćĺ   - Presents human-readable runtime status (for example terminal output, dashboard, or other\n    99Ôćĺ     operator-facing view).\n   100Ôćĺ\n   101Ôćĺ8. `Logging`\n   102Ôćĺ   - Emits structured runtime logs to one or more configured sinks.\n   103Ôćĺ\n   104Ôćĺ### 3.2 Abstraction Levels\n   105Ôćĺ\n   106ÔćĺSymphony is easiest to port when kept in these layers:\n   107Ôćĺ\n   108Ôćĺ1. `Policy Layer` (repo-defined)\n   109Ôćĺ   - `WORKFLOW.md` prompt body.\n   110Ôćĺ   - Team-specific rules for ticket handling, validation, and handoff.\n   111Ôćĺ\n   112Ôćĺ2. `Configuration Layer` (typed getters)\n   113Ôćĺ   - Parses front matter into typed runtime settings.\n   114Ôćĺ   - Handles defaults, environment tokens, and path normalization.\n   115Ôćĺ\n   116Ôćĺ3. `Coordination Layer` (orchestrator)\n   117Ôćĺ   - Polling loop, issue eligibility, concurrency, retries, reconciliation.\n   118Ôćĺ\n   119Ôćĺ4. `Execution Layer` (workspace + agent subprocess)\n   120Ôćĺ   - Filesystem lifecycle, workspace preparation, coding-agent protocol.\n   121Ôćĺ\n   122Ôćĺ5. `Integration Layer` (Linear adapter)\n   123Ôćĺ   - API calls and normalization for tracker data.\n   124Ôćĺ\n   125Ôćĺ6. `Observability Layer` (logs + optional status surface)\n   126Ôćĺ   - Operator visibility into orchestrator and agent behavior.\n   127Ôćĺ\n   128Ôćĺ### 3.3 External Dependencies\n   129Ôćĺ\n   130Ôćĺ- Issue tracker API (Linear for `tracker.kind: linear` in this specification version).\n   131Ôćĺ- Local filesystem for workspaces and logs.\n   132Ôćĺ- Optional workspace population tooling (for example Git CLI, if used).\n   133Ôćĺ- Coding-agent executable that supports JSON-RPC-like app-server mode over stdio.\n   134Ôćĺ- Host environment authentication for the issue tracker and coding agent.\n   135Ôćĺ\n   136Ôćĺ## 4. Core Domain Model\n   137Ôćĺ\n   138Ôćĺ### 4.1 Entities\n   139Ôćĺ\n   140Ôćĺ#### 4.1.1 Issue\n   141Ôćĺ\n   142ÔćĺNormalized issue record used by orchestration, prompt rendering, and observability output.\n   143Ôćĺ\n   144ÔćĺFields:\n   145Ôćĺ\n   146Ôćĺ- `id` (string)\n   147Ôćĺ  - Stable tracker-internal ID.\n   148Ôćĺ- `identifier` (string)\n   149Ôćĺ  - Human-readable ticket key (example: `ABC-123`).\n   150Ôćĺ- `title` (string)\n   151Ôćĺ- `description` (string or null)\n   152Ôćĺ- `priority` (integer or null)\n   153Ôćĺ  - Lower numbers are higher priority in dispatch sorting.\n   154Ôćĺ- `state` (string)\n   155Ôćĺ  - Current tracker state name.\n   156Ôćĺ- `branch_name` (string or null)\n   157Ôćĺ  - Tracker-provided branch metadata if available.\n   158Ôćĺ- `url` (string or null)\n   159Ôćĺ- `labels` (list of strings)\n   160Ôćĺ  - Normalized to lowercase.\n   161Ôćĺ- `blocked_by` (list of blocker refs)\n   162Ôćĺ  - Each blocker ref contains:\n   163Ôćĺ    - `id` (string or null)\n   164Ôćĺ    - `identifier` (string or null)\n   165Ôćĺ    - `state` (string or null)\n   166Ôćĺ- `created_at` (timestamp or null)\n   167Ôćĺ- `updated_at` (timestamp or null)\n   168Ôćĺ\n   169Ôćĺ#### 4.1.2 Workflow Definition\n   170Ôćĺ\n   171ÔćĺParsed `WORKFLOW.md` payload:\n   172Ôćĺ\n   173Ôćĺ- `config` (map)\n   174Ôćĺ  - YAML front matter root object.\n   175Ôćĺ- `prompt_template` (string)\n   176Ôćĺ  - Markdown body after front matter, trimmed.\n   177Ôćĺ\n   178Ôćĺ#### 4.1.3 Service Config (Typed View)\n   179Ôćĺ\n   180ÔćĺTyped runtime values derived from `WorkflowDefinition.config` plus environment resolution.\n   181Ôćĺ\n   182ÔćĺExamples:\n   183Ôćĺ\n   184Ôćĺ- poll interval\n   185Ôćĺ- workspace root\n   186Ôćĺ- active and terminal issue states\n   187Ôćĺ- concurrency limits\n   188Ôćĺ- coding-agent executable/args/timeouts\n   189Ôćĺ- workspace hooks\n   190Ôćĺ\n   191Ôćĺ#### 4.1.4 Workspace\n   192Ôćĺ\n   193ÔćĺFilesystem workspace assigned to one issue identifier.\n   194Ôćĺ\n   195ÔćĺFields (logical):\n   196Ôćĺ\n   197Ôćĺ- `path` (workspace path; current runtime typically uses absolute paths, but relative roots are\n   198Ôćĺ  possible if configured without path separators)\n   199Ôćĺ- `workspace_key` (sanitized issue identifier)\n   200Ôćĺ- `created_now` (boolean, used to gate `after_create` hook)\n   201Ôćĺ\n   202Ôćĺ#### 4.1.5 Run Attempt\n   203Ôćĺ\n   204ÔćĺOne execution attempt for one issue.\n   205Ôćĺ\n   206ÔćĺFields (logical):\n   207Ôćĺ\n   208Ôćĺ- `issue_id`\n   209Ôćĺ- `issue_identifier`\n   210Ôćĺ- `attempt` (integer or null, `null` for first run, `>=1` for retries/continuation)\n   211Ôćĺ- `workspace_path`\n   212Ôćĺ- `started_at`\n   213Ôćĺ- `status`\n   214Ôćĺ- `error` (optional)\n   215Ôćĺ\n   216Ôćĺ#### 4.1.6 Live Session (Agent Session Metadata)\n   217Ôćĺ\n   218ÔćĺState tracked while a coding-agent subprocess is running.\n   219Ôćĺ\n   220ÔćĺFields:\n   221Ôćĺ\n   222Ôćĺ- `session_id` (string, `<thread_id>-<turn_id>`)\n   223Ôćĺ- `thread_id` (string)\n   224Ôćĺ- `turn_id` (string)\n   225Ôćĺ- `codex_app_server_pid` (string or null)\n   226Ôćĺ- `last_codex_event` (string/enum or null)\n   227Ôćĺ- `last_codex_timestamp` (timestamp or null)\n   228Ôćĺ- `last_codex_message` (summarized payload)\n   229Ôćĺ- `codex_input_tokens` (integer)\n   230Ôćĺ- `codex_output_tokens` (integer)\n   231Ôćĺ- `codex_total_tokens` (integer)\n   232Ôćĺ- `last_reported_input_tokens` (integer)\n   233Ôćĺ- `last_reported_output_tokens` (integer)\n   234Ôćĺ- `last_reported_total_tokens` (integer)\n   235Ôćĺ- `turn_count` (integer)\n   236Ôćĺ  - Number of coding-agent turns started within the current worker lifetime.\n   237Ôćĺ\n   238Ôćĺ#### 4.1.7 Retry Entry\n   239Ôćĺ\n   240ÔćĺScheduled retry state for an issue.\n   241Ôćĺ\n   242ÔćĺFields:\n   243Ôćĺ\n   244Ôćĺ- `issue_id`\n   245Ôćĺ- `identifier` (best-effort human ID for status surfaces/logs)\n   246Ôćĺ- `attempt` (integer, 1-based for retry queue)\n   247Ôćĺ- `due_at_ms` (monotonic clock timestamp)\n   248Ôćĺ- `timer_handle` (runtime-specific timer reference)\n   249Ôćĺ- `error` (string or null)\n   250Ôćĺ\n   251Ôćĺ#### 4.1.8 Orchestrator Runtime State\n   252Ôćĺ\n   253ÔćĺSingle authoritative in-memory state owned by the orchestrator.\n   254Ôćĺ\n   255ÔćĺFields:\n   256Ôćĺ\n   257Ôćĺ- `poll_interval_ms` (current effective poll interval)\n   258Ôćĺ- `max_concurrent_agents` (current effective global concurrency limit)\n   259Ôćĺ- `running` (map `issue_id -> running entry`)\n   260Ôćĺ- `claimed` (set of issue IDs reserved/running/retrying)\n   261Ôćĺ- `retry_attempts` (map `issue_id -> RetryEntry`)\n   262Ôćĺ- `completed` (set of issue IDs; bookkeeping only, not dispatch gating)\n   263Ôćĺ- `codex_totals` (aggregate tokens + runtime seconds)\n   264Ôćĺ- `codex_rate_limits` (latest rate-limit snapshot from agent events)\n   265Ôćĺ\n   266Ôćĺ### 4.2 Stable Identifiers and Normalization Rules\n   267Ôćĺ\n   268Ôćĺ- `Issue ID`\n   269Ôćĺ  - Use for tracker lookups and internal map keys.\n   270Ôćĺ- `Issue Identifier`\n   271Ôćĺ  - Use for human-readable logs and workspace naming.\n   272Ôćĺ- `Workspace Key`\n   273Ôćĺ  - Derive from `issue.identifier` by replacing any character not in `[A-Za-z0-9._-]` with `_`.\n   274Ôćĺ  - Use the sanitized value for the workspace directory name.\n   275Ôćĺ- `Normalized Issue State`\n   276Ôćĺ  - Compare states after `lowercase`.\n   277Ôćĺ- `Session ID`\n   278Ôćĺ  - Compose from coding-agent `thread_id` and `turn_id` as `<thread_id>-<turn_id>`.\n   279Ôćĺ\n   280Ôćĺ## 5. Workflow Specification (Repository Contract)\n   281Ôćĺ\n   282Ôćĺ### 5.1 File Discovery and Path Resolution\n   283Ôćĺ\n   284ÔćĺWorkflow file path precedence:\n   285Ôćĺ\n   286Ôćĺ1. Explicit application/runtime setting (set by CLI startup path).\n   287Ôćĺ2. Default: `WORKFLOW.md` in the current process working directory.\n   288Ôćĺ\n   289ÔćĺLoader behavior:\n   290Ôćĺ\n   291Ôćĺ- If the file cannot be read, return `missing_workflow_file` error.\n   292Ôćĺ- The workflow file is expected to be repository-owned and version-controlled.\n   293Ôćĺ\n   294Ôćĺ### 5.2 File Format\n   295Ôćĺ\n   296Ôćĺ`WORKFLOW.md` is a Markdown file with optional YAML front matter.\n   297Ôćĺ\n   298ÔćĺDesign note:\n   299Ôćĺ\n   300Ôćĺ- `WORKFLOW.md` should be self-contained enough to describe and run different workflows (prompt,\n   301Ôćĺ  runtime settings, hooks, and tracker selection/config) without requiring out-of-band\n   302Ôćĺ  service-specific configuration.\n   303Ôćĺ\n   304ÔćĺParsing rules:\n   305Ôćĺ\n   306Ôćĺ- If file starts with `---`, parse lines until the next `---` as YAML front matter.\n   307Ôćĺ- Remaining lines become the prompt body.\n   308Ôćĺ- If front matter is absent, treat the entire file as prompt body and use an empty config map.\n   309Ôćĺ- YAML front matter must decode to a map/object; non-map YAML is an error.\n   310Ôćĺ- Prompt body is trimmed before use.\n   311Ôćĺ\n   312ÔćĺReturned workflow object:\n   313Ôćĺ\n   314Ôćĺ- `config`: front matter root object (not nested under a `config` key).\n   315Ôćĺ- `prompt_template`: trimmed Markdown body.\n   316Ôćĺ\n   317Ôćĺ### 5.3 Front Matter Schema\n   318Ôćĺ\n   319ÔćĺTop-level keys:\n   320Ôćĺ\n   321Ôćĺ- `tracker`\n   322Ôćĺ- `polling`\n   323Ôćĺ- `workspace`\n   324Ôćĺ- `hooks`\n   325Ôćĺ- `agent`\n   326Ôćĺ- `codex`\n   327Ôćĺ\n   328ÔćĺUnknown keys should be ignored for forward compatibility.\n   329Ôćĺ\n   330ÔćĺNote:\n   331Ôćĺ\n   332Ôćĺ- The workflow front matter is extensible. Optional extensions may define additional top-level keys\n   333Ôćĺ  (for example `server`) without changing the core schema above.\n   334Ôćĺ- Extensions should document their field schema, defaults, validation rules, and whether changes\n   335Ôćĺ  apply dynamically or require restart.\n   336Ôćĺ- Common extension: `server.port` (integer) enables the optional HTTP server described in Section\n   337Ôćĺ  13.7.\n   338Ôćĺ\n   339Ôćĺ#### 5.3.1 `tracker` (object)\n   340Ôćĺ\n   341ÔćĺFields:\n   342Ôćĺ\n   343Ôćĺ- `kind` (string)\n   344Ôćĺ  - Required for dispatch.\n   345Ôćĺ  - Current supported value: `linear`\n   346Ôćĺ- `endpoint` (string)\n   347Ôćĺ  - Default for `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`: `https://api.linear.app/graphql`\n   348Ôćĺ- `api_key` (string)\n   349Ôćĺ  - May be a literal token or `$VAR_NAME`.\n   350Ôćĺ  - Canonical environment variable for `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`: `LINEAR_API_KEY`.\n   351Ôćĺ  - If `$VAR_NAME` resolves to an empty string, treat the key as missing.\n   352Ôćĺ- `project_slug` (string)\n   353Ôćĺ  - Required for dispatch when `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`.\n   354Ôćĺ- `active_states` (list of strings)\n   355Ôćĺ  - Default: `Todo`, `In Progress`\n   356Ôćĺ- `terminal_states` (list of strings)\n   357Ôćĺ  - Default: `Closed`, `Cancelled`, `Canceled`, `Duplicate`, `Done`\n   358Ôćĺ\n   359Ôćĺ#### 5.3.2 `polling` (object)\n   360Ôćĺ\n   361ÔćĺFields:\n   362Ôćĺ\n   363Ôćĺ- `interval_ms` (integer or string integer)\n   364Ôćĺ  - Default: `30000`\n   365Ôćĺ  - Changes should be re-applied at runtime and affect future tick scheduling without restart.\n   366Ôćĺ\n   367Ôćĺ#### 5.3.3 `workspace` (object)\n   368Ôćĺ\n   369ÔćĺFields:\n   370Ôćĺ\n   371Ôćĺ- `root` (path string or `$VAR`)\n   372Ôćĺ  - Default: `<system-temp>/symphony_workspaces`\n   373Ôćĺ  - `~` and strings containing path separators are expanded.\n   374Ôćĺ  - Bare strings without path separators are preserved as-is (relative roots are allowed but\n   375Ôćĺ    discouraged).\n   376Ôćĺ\n   377Ôćĺ#### 5.3.4 `hooks` (object)\n   378Ôćĺ\n   379ÔćĺFields:\n   380Ôćĺ\n   381Ôćĺ- `after_create` (multiline shell script string, optional)\n   382Ôćĺ  - Runs only when a workspace directory is newly created.\n   383Ôćĺ  - Failure aborts workspace creation.\n   384Ôćĺ- `before_run` (multiline shell script string, optional)\n   385Ôćĺ  - Runs before each agent attempt after workspace preparation and before launching the coding\n   386Ôćĺ    agent.\n   387Ôćĺ  - To inspect the installed Codex schema, run\n   424Ôćĺ`codex app-server generate-json-schema --out <dir>` and inspect the relevant definitions referenced\n   425Ôćĺby `v2/ThreadStartParams.json` and `v2/TurnStartParams.json`. The runtime launches this command via `bash -lc` in the workspace directory.\n   431Ôćĺ  - The launched process must speak a compatible app-server protocol over stdio.\n   432Ôćĺ- `approval_policy` (Codex `AskForApproval` value)\n   433Ôćĺ  - Default: implementation-defined.\n   434Ôćĺ- `thread_sandbox` (Codex `SandboxMode` value)\n   435Ôćĺ  - Default: implementation-defined.\n   436Ôćĺ- `turn_sandbox_policy` (Codex `SandboxPolicy` value)\n   437Ôćĺ  - Default: implementation-defined.\n   438Ôćĺ- `turn_timeout_ms` (integer)\n   439Ôćĺ  - Default: `3600000` (1 hour)\n   440Ôćĺ- `read_timeout_ms` (integer)\n   441Ôćĺ  - Default: `5000`\n   442Ôćĺ- `stall_timeout_ms` (integer)\n   443Ôćĺ  - Default: `300000` (5 minutes)\n   444Ôćĺ  - If `<= 0`, stall detection is disabled.\n   445Ôćĺ\n   446Ôćĺ### 5.4 Prompt Template Contract\n   447Ôćĺ\n   448ÔćĺThe Markdown body of `WORKFLOW.md` is the per-issue prompt template.\n   449Ôćĺ\n   450ÔćĺRendering requirements:\n   451Ôćĺ\n   452Ôćĺ- Use a strict template engine (Liquid-compatible semantics are sufficient).\n   453Ôćĺ- Unknown variables must fail rendering.\n   454Ôćĺ- Unknown filters must fail rendering.\n   455Ôćĺ\n   456ÔćĺTemplate input variables:\n   457Ôćĺ\n   458Ôćĺ- `issue` (object)\n   459Ôćĺ  - Includes all normalized issue fields, including labels and blockers.\n   460Ôćĺ- `attempt` (integer or null)\n   461Ôćĺ  - `null`/absent on first attempt.\n   462Ôćĺ  - Integer on retry or continuation run.\n   463Ôćĺ\n   464ÔćĺFallback prompt behavior:\n   465Ôćĺ\n   466Ôćĺ- If the workflow prompt body is empty, the runtime may use a minimal default prompt\n   467Ôćĺ  (`You are working on an issue from Linear.`).\n   468Ôćĺ- Workflow file read/parse failures are configuration/validation errors and should not silently fall\n   469Ôćĺ  back to a prompt.\n   470Ôćĺ\n   471Ôćĺ### 5.5 Workflow Validation and Error Surface\n   472Ôćĺ\n   473ÔćĺError classes:\n   474Ôćĺ\n   475Ôćĺ- `missing_workflow_file`\n   476Ôćĺ- `workflow_parse_error`\n   477Ôćĺ- `workflow_front_matter_not_a_map`\n   478Ôćĺ- `template_parse_error` (during prompt rendering)\n   479Ôćĺ- `template_render_error` (unknown variable/filter, invalid interpolation)\n   480Ôćĺ\n   481ÔćĺDispatch gating behavior:\n   482Ôćĺ\n   483Ôćĺ- Workflow file read/YAML errors block new dispatches until fixed.\n   484Ôćĺ- Template errors fail only the affected run attempt.\n   485Ôćĺ\n   486Ôćĺ## 6. Configuration Specification\n   487Ôćĺ\n   488Ôćĺ### 6.1 Source Precedence and Resolution Semantics\n   489Ôćĺ\n   490ÔćĺConfiguration precedence:\n   491Ôćĺ\n   492Ôćĺ1. Workflow file path selection (runtime setting -> cwd default).\n   493Ôćĺ2. YAML front matter values.\n   494Ôćĺ3. Environment indirection via `$VAR_NAME` inside selected YAML values.\n   495Ôćĺ4. Built-in defaults.\n   496Ôćĺ\n   497ÔćĺValue coercion semantics:\n   498Ôćĺ\n   499Ôćĺ- Path/command fields support:\n   500Ôćĺ  - `~` home expansion\n   501Ôćĺ  - `$VAR` expansion for env-backed path values\n   502Ôćĺ  - Apply expansion only to values intended to be local filesystem paths; do not rewrite URIs or\n   503Ôćĺ    arbitrary shell command strings.\n   504Ôćĺ\n   505Ôćĺ### 6.2 Dynamic Reload Semantics\n   506Ôćĺ\n   507ÔćĺDynamic reload is required:\n   508Ôćĺ\n   509Ôćĺ- The software should watch `WORKFLOW.md` for changes.\n   510Ôćĺ- On change, it should re-read and re-apply workflow config and prompt template without restart.\n   511Ôćĺ- The software should attempt to adjust live behavior to the new config (for example polling\n   512Ôćĺ  cadence, concurrency limits, active/terminal states, codex settings, workspace paths/hooks, and\n   513Ôćĺ  prompt content for future runs).\n   514Ôćĺ- Reloaded config applies to future dispatch, retry scheduling, reconciliation decisions, hook\n   515Ôćĺ  execution, and agent launches.\n   516Ôćĺ- Implementations are not required to restart in-flight agent sessions automatically when config\n   517Ôćĺ  changes.\n   518Ôćĺ- Extensions that manage their own listeners/resources (for example an HTTP server port change) may\n   519Ôćĺ  require restart unless the implementation explicitly supports live rebind.\n   520Ôćĺ- Implementations should also re-validate/reload defensively during runtime operations (for example\n   521Ôćĺ  before dispatch) in case filesystem watch events are missed.\n   522Ôćĺ- Invalid reloads should not crash the service; keep operating with the last known good effective\n   523Ôćĺ  configuration and emit an operator-visible error.\n   524Ôćĺ\n   525Ôćĺ### 6.3 Dispatch Preflight Validation\n   526Ôćĺ\n   527ÔćĺThis validation is a scheduler preflight run before attempting to dispatch new work. It validates\n   528Ôćĺthe workflow/config needed to poll and launch workers, not a full audit of all possible workflow\n   529Ôćĺbehavior.\n   530Ôćĺ\n   531ÔćĺStartup validation:\n   532Ôćĺ\n   533Ôćĺ- Validate configuration before starting the scheduling loop.\n   534Ôćĺ- If startup validation fails, fail startup and emit an operator-visible error.\n   535Ôćĺ\n   536ÔćĺPer-tick dispatch validation:\n   537Ôćĺ\n   538Ôćĺ- Re-validate before each dispatch cycle.\n   539Ôćĺ- If validation fails, skip dispatch for that tick, keep reconciliation active, and emit an\n   540Ôćĺ  operator-visible error.\n   541Ôćĺ\n   542ÔćĺValidation checks:\n   543Ôćĺ\n   544Ôćĺ- Workflow file can be loaded and parsed.\n   545Ôćĺ- `tracker.kind` is present and supported.\n   546Ôćĺ- `tracker.api_key` is present after `$` resolution.\n   547Ôćĺ- `tracker.project_slug` is present when required by the selected tracker kind.\n   548Ôćĺ- `codex.command` is present and non-empty.\n   549Ôćĺ\n   550Ôćĺ### 6.4 Config Fields Summary (Cheat Sheet)\n   551Ôćĺ\n   552ÔćĺThis section is intentionally redundant so a coding agent can implement the config layer quickly.\n   553Ôćĺ\n   554Ôćĺ- `tracker.kind`: string, required, currently `linear`\n   555Ôćĺ- `tracker.endpoint`: string, default `https://api.linear.app/graphql` when `tracker.kind=linear`\n   556Ôćĺ- `tracker.api_key`: string or `$VAR`, canonical env `LINEAR_API_KEY` when `tracker.kind=linear`\n   557Ôćĺ- `tracker.project_slug`: string, required when `tracker.kind=linear`\n   558Ôćĺ- `tracker.active_states`: list of strings, default `[\"Todo\", \"In Progress\"]`\n   559Ôćĺ- `tracker.terminal_states`: list of strings, default `[\"Closed\", \"Cancelled\", \"Canceled\", \"Duplicate\", \"Done\"]`\n   560Ôćĺ- `polling.interval_ms`: integer, default `30000`\n   561Ôćĺ- `workspace.root`: path, default `<system-temp>/symphony_workspaces`\n   562Ôćĺ- `worker.ssh_hosts` (extension): list of SSH host strings, optional; when omitted, work runs\n   563Ôćĺ  locally\n   564Ôćĺ- `worker.max_concurrent_agents_per_host` (extension): positive integer, optional; shared per-host\n   565Ôćĺ  cap applied across configured SSH hosts\n   566Ôćĺ- `hooks.after_create`: shell script or null\n   567Ôćĺ- `hooks.before_run`: shell script or null\n   568Ôćĺ- `hooks.after_run`: shell script or null\n   569Ôćĺ- `hooks.before_remove`: shell script or null\n   570Ôćĺ- `hooks.timeout_ms`: integer, default `60000`\n   571Ôćĺ- `agent.max_concurrent_agents`: integer, default `10`\n   572Ôćĺ- `agent.max_turns`: integer, default `20`\n   573Ôćĺ- `agent.max_retry_backoff_ms`: integer, default `300000` (5m)\n   574Ôćĺ- `agent.max_concurrent_agents_by_state`: map of positive integers, default `{}`\n   575Ôćĺ- `codex.command`: shell command string, default `codex app-server`\n   576Ôćĺ- `codex.approval_policy`: Codex `AskForApproval` value, default implementation-defined\n   577Ôćĺ- `codex.thread_sandbox`: Codex `SandboxMode` value, default implementation-defined\n   578Ôćĺ- `codex.turn_sandbox_policy`: Codex `SandboxPolicy` value, default implementation-defined\n   579Ôćĺ- `codex.turn_timeout_ms`: integer, default `3600000`\n   580Ôćĺ- `codex.read_timeout_ms`: integer, default `5000`\n   581Ôćĺ- `codex.stall_timeout_ms`: integer, default `300000`\n   582Ôćĺ- `server.port` (extension): integer, optional; enables the optional HTTP server, `0` may be used\n   583Ôćĺ  for ephemeral local bind, and CLI `--port` overrides it\n   584Ôćĺ\n   585Ôćĺ## 7. Orchestration State Machine\n   586Ôćĺ\n   587ÔćĺThe orchestrator is the only component that mutates scheduling state. All worker outcomes are\n   588Ôćĺreported back to it and converted into explicit state transitions.\n   589Ôćĺ\n   590Ôćĺ### 7.1 Issue Orchestration States\n   591Ôćĺ\n   592ÔćĺThis is not the same as tracker states (`Todo`, `In Progress`, etc.). This is the service's internal\n   593Ôćĺclaim state.\n   594Ôćĺ\n   595Ôćĺ1. `Unclaimed`\n   596Ôćĺ   - Issue is not running and has no retry scheduled.\n   597Ôćĺ\n   598Ôćĺ2. `Claimed`\n   599Ôćĺ   - Orchestrator has reserved the issue to prevent duplicate dispatch.\n   600Ôćĺ   - In practice, claimed issues are either `Running` or `RetryQueued`.\n   601Ôćĺ\n   602Ôćĺ3. `Running`\n   603Ôćĺ   - Worker task exists and the issue is tracked in `running` map.\n   604Ôćĺ\n   605Ôćĺ4. `RetryQueued`\n   606Ôćĺ   - Worker is not running, but a retry timer exists in `retry_attempts`.\n   607Ôćĺ\n   608Ôćĺ5. `Released`\n   609Ôćĺ   - Claim removed because issue is terminal, non-active, missing, or retry path completed without\n   610Ôćĺ     re-dispatch.\n   611Ôćĺ\n   612ÔćĺImportant nuance:\n   613Ôćĺ\n   614Ôćĺ- A successful worker exit does not mean the issue is done forever.\n   615Ôćĺ- The worker may continue through multiple back-to-back coding-agent turns before it exits.\n   616Ôćĺ- After each normal turn completion, the worker re-checks the tracker issue state.\n   617Ôćĺ- If the issue is still in an active state, the worker should start another turn on the same live\n   618Ôćĺ  coding-agent thread in the same workspace, up to `agent.max_turns`.\n   619Ôćĺ- The first turn should use the full rendered task prompt.\n   620Ôćĺ- Continuation turns should send only continuation guidance to the existing thread, not resend the\n   621Ôćĺ  original task prompt that is already present in thread history.\n   622Ôćĺ- Once the worker exits normally, the orchestrator still schedules a short continuation retry\n   623Ôćĺ  (about 1 second) so it can re-check whether the issue remains active and needs another worker\n   624Ôćĺ  session.\n   625Ôćĺ\n   626Ôćĺ### 7.2 Run Attempt Lifecycle\n   627Ôćĺ\n   628ÔćĺA run attempt transitions through these phases:\n   629Ôćĺ\n   630Ôćĺ1. `PreparingWorkspace`\n   631Ôćĺ2. `BuildingPrompt`\n   632Ôćĺ3. `LaunchingAgentProcess`\n   633Ôćĺ4. `InitializingSession`\n   634Ôćĺ5. `StreamingTurn`\n   635Ôćĺ6. `Finishing`\n   636Ôćĺ7. `Succeeded`\n   637Ôćĺ8. `Failed`\n   638Ôćĺ9. `TimedOut`\n   639Ôćĺ10. `Stalled`\n   640Ôćĺ11. `CanceledByReconciliation`\n   641Ôćĺ\n   642ÔćĺDistinct terminal reasons are important because retry logic and logs differ.\n   643Ôćĺ\n   644Ôćĺ### 7.3 Transition Triggers\n   645Ôćĺ\n   646Ôćĺ- `Poll Tick`\n   647Ôćĺ  - Reconcile active runs.\n   648Ôćĺ  - Validate config.\n   649Ôćĺ  - Fetch candidate issues.\n   650Ôćĺ  - Dispatch until slots are exhausted.\n   651Ôćĺ\n   652Ôćĺ- `Worker Exit (normal)`\n   653Ôćĺ  - Remove running entry.\n   654Ôćĺ  - Update aggregate runtime totals.\n   655Ôćĺ  - Schedule continuation retry (attempt `1`) after the worker exhausts or finishes its in-process\n   656Ôćĺ    turn loop.\n   657Ôćĺ\n   658Ôćĺ- `Worker Exit (abnormal)`\n   659Ôćĺ  - Remove running entry.\n   660Ôćĺ  - Update aggregate runtime totals.\n   661Ôćĺ  - Schedule exponential-backoff retry.\n   662Ôćĺ\n   663Ôćĺ- `Codex Update Event`\n   664Ôćĺ  - Update live session fields, token counters, and rate limits.\n   665Ôćĺ\n   666Ôćĺ- `Retry Timer Fired`\n   667Ôćĺ  - Re-fetch active candidates and attempt re-dispatch, or release claim if no longer eligible.\n   668Ôćĺ\n   669Ôćĺ- `Reconciliation State Refresh`\n   670Ôćĺ  - Stop runs whose issue states are terminal or no longer active.\n   671Ôćĺ\n   672Ôćĺ- `Stall Timeout`\n   673Ôćĺ  - Kill worker and schedule retry.\n   674Ôćĺ\n   675Ôćĺ### 7.4 Idempotency and Recovery Rules\n   676Ôćĺ\n   677Ôćĺ- The orchestrator serializes state mutations through one authority to avoid duplicate dispatch.\n   678Ôćĺ- `claimed` and `running` checks are required before launching any worker.\n   679Ôćĺ- Reconciliation runs before dispatch on every tick.\n   680Ôćĺ- Restart recovery is tracker-driven and filesystem-driven (no durable orchestrator DB required).\n   681Ôćĺ- Startup terminal cleanup removes stale workspaces for issues already in terminal states.\n   682Ôćĺ\n   683Ôćĺ## 8. Polling, Scheduling, and Reconciliation\n   684Ôćĺ\n   685Ôćĺ### 8.1 Poll Loop\n   686Ôćĺ\n   687ÔćĺAt startup, the service validates config, performs startup cleanup, schedules an immediate tick, and\n   688Ôćĺthen repeats every `polling.interval_ms`.\n   689Ôćĺ\n   690ÔćĺThe effective poll interval should be updated when workflow config changes are re-applied.\n   691Ôćĺ\n   692ÔćĺTick sequence:\n   693Ôćĺ\n   694Ôćĺ1. Reconcile running issues.\n   695Ôćĺ2. Run dispatch preflight validation.\n   696Ôćĺ3. Fetch candidate issues from tracker using active states.\n   697Ôćĺ4. Sort issues by dispatch priority.\n   698Ôćĺ5. Dispatch eligible issues while slots remain.\n   699Ôćĺ6. Notify observability/status consumers of state changes.\n   700Ôćĺ\n   701ÔćĺIf per-tick validation fails, dispatch is skipped for that tick, but reconciliation still happens\n   702Ôćĺfirst.\n   703Ôćĺ\n   704Ôćĺ### 8.2 Candidate Selection Rules\n   705Ôćĺ\n   706ÔćĺAn issue is dispatch-eligible only if all are true:\n   707Ôćĺ\n   708Ôćĺ- It has `id`, `identifier`, `title`, and `state`.\n   709Ôćĺ- Its state is in `active_states` and not in `terminal_states`.\n   710Ôćĺ- It is not already in `running`.\n   711Ôćĺ- It is not already in `claimed`.\n   712Ôćĺ- Global concurrency slots are available.\n   713Ôćĺ- Per-state concurrency slots are available.\n   714Ôćĺ- Blocker rule for `Todo` state passes:\n   715Ôćĺ  - If the issue state is `Todo`, do not dispatch when any blocker is non-terminal.\n   716Ôćĺ\n   717ÔćĺSorting order (stable intent):\n   718Ôćĺ\n   719Ôćĺ1. `priority` ascending (1..4 are preferred; null/unknown sorts last)\n   720Ôćĺ2. `created_at` oldest first\n   721Ôćĺ3. `identifier` lexicographic tie-breaker\n   722Ôćĺ\n   723Ôćĺ### 8.3 Concurrency Control\n   724Ôćĺ\n   725ÔćĺGlobal limit:\n   726Ôćĺ\n   727Ôćĺ- `available_slots = max(max_concurrent_agents - running_count, 0)`\n   728Ôćĺ\n   729ÔćĺPer-state limit:\n   730Ôćĺ\n   731Ôćĺ- `max_concurrent_agents_by_state[state]` if present (state key normalized)\n   732Ôćĺ- otherwise fallback to global limit\n   733Ôćĺ\n   734ÔćĺThe runtime counts issues by their current tracked state in the `running` map.\n   735Ôćĺ\n   736ÔćĺOptional SSH host limit:\n   737Ôćĺ\n   738Ôćĺ- When `worker.max_concurrent_agents_per_host` is set, each configured SSH host may run at most\n   739Ôćĺ  that many concurrent agents at once.\n   740Ôćĺ- Hosts at that cap are skipped for new dispatch until capacity frees up.\n   741Ôćĺ\n   742Ôćĺ### 8.4 Retry and Backoff\n   743Ôćĺ\n   744ÔćĺRetry entry creation:\n   745Ôćĺ\n   746Ôćĺ- Cancel any existing retry timer for the same issue.\n   747Ôćĺ- Store `attempt`, `identifier`, `error`, `due_at_ms`, and new timer handle.\n   748Ôćĺ\n   749ÔćĺBackoff formula:\n   750Ôćĺ\n   751Ôćĺ- Normal continuation retries after a clean worker exit use a short fixed delay of `1000` ms.\n   752Ôćĺ- Failure-driven retries use `delay = min(10000 * 2^(attempt - 1), agent.max_retry_backoff_ms)`.\n   753Ôćĺ- Power is capped by the configured max retry backoff (default `300000` / 5m).\n   754Ôćĺ\n   755ÔćĺRetry handling behavior:\n   756Ôćĺ\n   757Ôćĺ1. Fetch active candidate issues (not all issues).\n   758Ôćĺ2. Find the specific issue by `issue_id`.\n   759Ôćĺ3. If not found, release claim.\n   760Ôćĺ4. If found and still candidate-eligible:\n   761Ôćĺ   - Dispatch if slots are available.\n   762Ôćĺ   - Otherwise requeue with error `no available orchestrator slots`.\n   763Ôćĺ5. If found but no longer active, release claim.\n   764Ôćĺ\n   765ÔćĺNote:\n   766Ôćĺ\n   767Ôćĺ- Terminal-state workspace cleanup is handled by startup cleanup and active-run reconciliation\n   768Ôćĺ  (including terminal transitions for currently running issues).\n   769Ôćĺ- Retry handling mainly operates on active candidates and releases claims when the issue is absent,\n   770Ôćĺ  rather than performing terminal cleanup itself.\n   771Ôćĺ\n   772Ôćĺ### 8.5 Active Run Reconciliation\n   773Ôćĺ\n   774ÔćĺReconciliation runs every tick and has two parts.\n   775Ôćĺ\n   776ÔćĺPart A: Stall detection\n   777Ôćĺ\n   778Ôćĺ- For each running issue, compute `elapsed_ms` since:\n   779Ôćĺ  - `last_codex_timestamp` if any event has been seen, else\n   780Ôćĺ  - `started_at`\n   781Ôćĺ- If `elapsed_ms > codex.stall_timeout_ms`, terminate the worker and queue a retry.\n   782Ôćĺ- If `stall_timeout_ms <= 0`, skip stall detection entirely.\n   783Ôćĺ\n   784ÔćĺPart B: Tracker state refresh\n   785Ôćĺ\n   786Ôćĺ- Fetch current issue states for all running issue IDs.\n   787Ôćĺ- For each running issue:\n   788Ôćĺ  - If tracker state is terminal: terminate worker and clean workspace.\n   789Ôćĺ  - If tracker state is still active: update the in-memory issue snapshot.\n   790Ôćĺ  - If tracker state is neither active nor terminal: terminate worker without workspace cleanup.\n   791Ôćĺ- If state refresh fails, keep workers running and try again on the next tick.\n   792Ôćĺ\n   793Ôćĺ### 8.6 Startup Terminal Workspace Cleanup\n   794Ôćĺ\n   795ÔćĺWhen the service starts:\n   796Ôćĺ\n   797Ôćĺ1. Query tracker for issues in terminal states.\n   798Ôćĺ2. For each returned issue identifier, remove the corresponding workspace directory.\n   799Ôćĺ3. If the terminal-issues fetch fails, log a warning and continue startup.\n   800Ôćĺ\n   801ÔćĺThis prevents stale terminal workspaces from accumulating after restarts.\n   802Ôćĺ\n   803Ôćĺ## 9. Workspace Management and Safety\n   804Ôćĺ\n   805Ôćĺ### 9.1 Workspace Layout\n   806Ôćĺ\n   807ÔćĺWorkspace root:\n   808Ôćĺ\n   809Ôćĺ- `workspace.root` (normalized path; the current config layer expands path-like values and preserves\n   810Ôćĺ  bare relative names)\n   811Ôćĺ\n   812ÔćĺPer-issue workspace path:\n   813Ôćĺ\n   814Ôćĺ- `<workspace.root>/<sanitized_issue_identifier>`\n   815Ôćĺ\n   816ÔćĺWorkspace persistence:\n   817Ôćĺ\n   818Ôćĺ- Workspaces are reused across runs for the same issue.\n   819Ôćĺ- Successful runs do not auto-delete workspaces.\n   820Ôćĺ\n   821Ôćĺ### 9.2 Workspace Creation and Reuse\n   822Ôćĺ\n   823ÔćĺInput: `issue.identifier`\n   824Ôćĺ\n   825ÔćĺAlgorithm summary:\n   826Ôćĺ\n   827Ôćĺ1. Sanitize identifier to `workspace_key`.\n   828Ôćĺ2. Compute workspace path under workspace root.\n   829Ôćĺ3. Ensure the workspace path exists as a directory.\n   830Ôćĺ4. Mark `created_now=true` only if the directory was created during this call; otherwise\n   831Ôćĺ   `created_now=false`.\n   832Ôćĺ5. If `created_now=true`, run `after_create` hook if configured.\n   833Ôćĺ\n   834ÔćĺNotes:\n   835Ôćĺ\n   836Ôćĺ- This section does not assume any specific repository/VCS workflow.\n   837Ôćĺ- Workspace preparation beyond directory creation (for example dependency bootstrap, checkout/sync,\n   838Ôćĺ  code generation) is implementation-defined and is typically handled via hooks.\n   839Ôćĺ\n   840Ôćĺ### 9.3 Optional Workspace Population (Implementation-Defined)\n   841Ôćĺ\n   842ÔćĺThe spec does not require any built-in VCS or repository bootstrap behavior.\n   843Ôćĺ\n   844ÔćĺImplementations may populate or synchronize the workspace using implementation-defined logic and/or\n   845Ôćĺhooks (for example `after_create` and/or `before_run`).\n   846Ôćĺ\n   847ÔćĺFailure handling:\n   848Ôćĺ\n   849Ôćĺ- Workspace population/synchronization failures return an error for the current attempt.\n   850Ôćĺ- If failure happens while creating a brand-new workspace, implementations may remove the partially\n   851Ôćĺ  prepared directory.\n   852Ôćĺ- Reused workspaces should not be destructively reset on population failure unless that policy is\n   853Ôćĺ  explicitly chosen and documented.\n   854Ôćĺ\n   855Ôćĺ### 9.4 Workspace Hooks\n   856Ôćĺ\n   857ÔćĺSupported hooks:\n   858Ôćĺ\n   859Ôćĺ- `hooks.after_create`\n   860Ôćĺ- `hooks.before_run`\n   861Ôćĺ- `hooks.after_run`\n   862Ôćĺ- `hooks.before_remove`\n   863Ôćĺ\n   864ÔćĺExecution contract:\n   865Ôćĺ\n   866Ôćĺ- Execute in a local shell context appropriate to the host OS, with the workspace directory as\n   867Ôćĺ  `cwd`.\n   868Ôćĺ- On POSIX systems, `sh -lc <script>` (or a stricter equivalent such as `bash -lc <script>`) is a\n   869Ôćĺ  conforming default.\n   870Ôćĺ- Hook timeout uses `hooks.timeout_ms`; Agent Runner Protocol (Coding Agent Integration)\n   901Ôćĺ\n   902ÔćĺThis section defines the language-neutral contract for integrating a coding agent app-server.\n   903Ôćĺ\n   904ÔćĺCompatibility profile:\n   905Ôćĺ\n   906Ôćĺ- The normative contract is message ordering, required behaviors, and the logical fields that must\n   907Ôćĺ  be extracted (for example session IDs, completion state,  913Ôćĺ\n   914Ôćĺ### 10.1 Launch Contract\n   915Ôćĺ\n   916ÔćĺSubprocess launch parameters:\n   917Ôćĺ\n   918Ôćĺ- Command: `codex.command`\n   919Ôćĺ- Invocation: `bash -lc <codex.command>`\n   920Ôćĺ- Working directory: workspace path\n   921Ôćĺ- Stdout/stderr: separate streams\n   922Ôćĺ- Framing: line-delimited protocol messages on stdout (JSON-RPC-like JSON per line)\n   923Ôćĺ\n   924ÔćĺNotes:\n   925Ôćĺ\n   926Ôćĺ- The default command is `codex app-server`.\n   927Ôćĺ- Approval policy, cwd, and prompt are expressed in the protocol messages in Section 10.2.\n   928Ôćĺ\n shapes are acceptable if they preserve the same\n   940Ôćĺsemantics):\n   941Ôćĺ\n   942Ôćĺ```json\n   943Ôćĺ{\"id\":1,\"method\":\"initialize\",\"params\":{\"clientInfo\":{\"name\":\"symphony\",\"version\":\"1.0\"},\"capabilities\":{}}}\n   944Ôćĺ{\"method\":\"initialized\",\"params\":{}}\n   945Ôćĺ{\"id\":2,\"method\":\"thread/start\",\"params\":{\"approvalPolicy\":\"<implementation-defined>\",\"sandbox\":\"<implementation-defined>\",\"cwd\":\"/abs/workspace\"}}\n   946Ôćĺ{\"id\":3,\"method\":\"turn/start\",\"params\":{\"threadId\":\"<thread-id>\",\"input\":[{\"type\":\"text\",\"text\":\"<rendered Example\",\"approvalPolicy\":\"<implementation-defined>\",\"sandboxPolicy\":{\"type\":\"<implementation-defined>\"}}}\n   947Ôćĺ```\n   948Ôćĺ\n   949Ôćĺ1. `initialize` request\n   950Ôćĺ   - Params include:\n   951Ôćĺ     - `clientInfo` object (for example `{name, version}`)\n   952Ôćĺ     - `capabilities` object (may be empty)\n   953Ôćĺ   - If the targeted Codex app-server requires capability `<issue.identifier>: <issue.title>`\n   971Ôćĺ     - `approvalPolicy` = implementation-defined turn approval policy value\n   972Ôćĺ     - `sandboxPolicy` = implementation-defined object-form sandbox continuation turns inside one worker run\n   981Ôćĺ\n   982Ôćĺ### 10.3 Streaming Turn Processing\n   983Ôćĺ\n   984ÔćĺThe client reads line-delimited messages until the turn terminates.\n   985Ôćĺ\n   986ÔćĺCompletion conditions:\n   987Ôćĺ\n   988Ôćĺ- `turn/completed` -> success\n   989Ôćĺ- `turn/failed` -> failure\n   990Ôćĺ- `turn/cancelled` -> failure\n   991Ôćĺ- turn timeout (`turn_timeout_ms`) -> failure\n   992Ôćĺ- subprocess exit -> failure\n   993Ôćĺ\n   994ÔćĺContinuation processing:\n   995Ôćĺ\n   996Ôćĺ- If the worker decides to continue after a successful turn, it should issue another `turn/start`\n   997Ôćĺ  on the same live `threadId`.\n   998Ôćĺ- The app-server subprocess should remain alive across those continuation turns and be stopped only\n   999Ôćĺ  when the worker run is ending.\n  1000Ôćĺ\n  1001ÔćĺLine handling requirements:\n  1002Ôćĺ\n  1003Ôćĺ- Read protocol messages from stdout only.\n  1004Ôćĺ- Buffer partial stdout lines until newline arrives.\n  1005Ôćĺ- Attempt JSON parse on complete stdout lines.\n  1006Ôćĺ- Stderr is not part of the protocol stream:\n  1007Ôćĺ  - ignore it or log it as diagnostics\n  1008Ôćĺ  - do not attempt protocol JSON parsing on stderr\n  1009Ôćĺ\n  1010Ôćĺ### 10.4 Emitted Runtime Events (Upstream to Orchestrator)\n  1011Ôćĺ\n  1012ÔćĺThe app-server client emits structured events to the orchestrator callback. Each event should\n  1013Ôćĺinclude:\n  1014Ôćĺ\n  1015Ôćĺ- `event` (enum/string)\n  1016Ôćĺ- `timestamp` (UTC timestamp)\n  1017Ôćĺ- `codex_app_server_pid` (if available)\n  1018Ôćĺ- optional `usage` map (token counts)\n  1019Ôćĺ- payload fields as needed\n  1020Ôćĺ\n  1021ÔćĺImportant emitted events may include:\n  1022Ôćĺ\n  1023Ôćĺ- `session_started`\n  1024Ôćĺ- `startup_failed`\n  1025Ôćĺ- `turn_completed`\n  1026Ôćĺ- `turn_failed`\n  1027Ôćĺ- `turn_cancelled`\n  1028Ôćĺ- `turn_ended_with_error`\n  1029Ôćĺ- `turn_input_required`\n  1030Ôćĺ- `approval_auto_approved`\n  1031Ôćĺ- `unsupported_tool_call`\n  1032Ôćĺ- `notification`\n  1033Ôćĺ- `other_message`\n  1034Ôćĺ- `malformed`\n  1035Ôćĺ\n  1036Ôćĺ### 10.5 Approval, Tool Calls, and User Input Policy\n  1037Ôćĺ\n  1038ÔćĺApproval, sandbox, and user-input behavior is implementation-defined.\n  1039Ôćĺ\n  1040ÔćĺPolicy requirements:\n  1041Ôćĺ\n  1042Ôćĺ- Each implementation should document its chosen approval, sandbox, and operator-confirmation\n  1043Ôćĺ  posture.\n  1044Ôćĺ- Approval requests and user-input-required events must not leave a run stalled indefinitely. An\n  1045Ôćĺ  implementation should either satisfy them, surface them to an operator, auto-resolve them, or\n  1046Ôćĺ  fail the run according to its documented policy.\n  1047Ôćĺ\n  1048ÔćĺExample high-trust behavior:\n  1049Ôćĺ\n  1050Ôćĺ- Auto-approve command execution approvals for the session.\n  1051Ôćĺ- Auto-approve file-change approvals for the session.\n  1052Ôćĺ- Treat user-input-required turns as hard failure.\n  1053Ôćĺ\n  1054ÔćĺUnsupported dynamic tool calls:\n  1055Ôćĺ\n  1056Ôćĺ- Supported dynamic tool calls that are explicitly implemented and advertised by the runtime should\n  1057Ôćĺ  be handled according to their extension contract.\n  1058Ôćĺ- If the agent requests a dynamic tool call (`item/tool/call`) that is not supported, return a tool\n  1059Ôćĺ  failure response and continue the session.\n  1060Ôćĺ- This prevents the session from stalling on unsupported tool execution paths.\n  1061Ôćĺ\n  1062ÔćĺOptional client-side tool extension:\n  1063Ôćĺ\n  1064Ôćĺ- An implementation may expose a limited set of client-side tools to the app-server session.\n  1065Ôćĺ- Current optional standardized tool: `linear_graphql`.\n  1066Ôćĺ- If Unsupported tool names should still return a failure result and continue the session.\n  1069Ôćĺ\n  1070Ôćĺ`linear_graphql` extension contract:\n  1071Ôćĺ\n  1072Ôćĺ- Purpose: execute a raw GraphQL query or mutation against Linear using Symphony's configured\n  1073Ôćĺ  tracker auth for the current session.\n  1074Ôćĺ- Availability: only meaningful when `tracker.kind == \"linear\"` and valid Linear auth is configured.\n  1075Ôćĺ- Preferred input shape:\n  1076Ôćĺ\n  1077Ôćĺ  ```json\n  1078Ôćĺ  {\n  1079Ôćĺ    \"query\": \"single GraphQL query or mutation document\",\n  1080Ôćĺ    \"variables\": {\n  1081Ôćĺ      \"optional\": \"graphql variables object\"\n  1082Ôćĺ    }\n  1083Ôćĺ  }\n  1084Ôćĺ  ```\n  1085Ôćĺ\n  1086Ôćĺ- `query` must be a non-empty string.\n  1087Ôćĺ- `query` must contain exactly one GraphQL operation.\n  1088Ôćĺ- `variables` is optional and, when present, must be a JSON object.\n  1089Ôćĺ- Implementations may additionally accept a raw GraphQL query string as shorthand input.\n  1090Ôćĺ- Execute one GraphQL operation per tool call.\n  1091Ôćĺ- If the provided document contains multiple operations, reject the tool call as invalid input.\n  1092Ôćĺ- `operationName` selection is intentionally out of scope for this extension.\n  1093Ôćĺ- Reuse the configured Linear endpoint and auth from the active Symphony workflow/runtime config; do\n  1094Ôćĺ  not require the coding agent to read raw tokens from disk.\n  1095Ôćĺ- Tool result semantics:\n  1096Ôćĺ  - transport success + no top-level GraphQL `errors` -> `success=true`\n  1097Ôćĺ  - top-level GraphQL `errors` present -> `success=false`, but preserve the GraphQL response body\n  1098Ôćĺ    for debugging\n  1099Ôćĺ  - invalid input, missing auth, or transport failure -> `success=false` with an error payload\n  1100Ôćĺ- Return the GraphQL response or error payload as structured tool output that the model can inspect\n  1101Ôćĺ  in-session.\n  1102Ôćĺ\n  1103ÔćĺIllustrative responses (equivalent payload shapes are acceptable if they preserve the same outcome):\n  1104Ôćĺ\n  1105Ôćĺ```json\n  1106Ôćĺ{\"id\":\"<approval-id>\",\"result\":{\"approved\":true}}\n  1107Ôćĺ{\"id\":\"<tool-call-id>\",\"result\":{\"success\":false,\"error\":\"unsupported_tool_call\"}}\n  1108Ôćĺ```\n  1109Ôćĺ\n  1110ÔćĺHard failure on user input requirement:\n  1111Ôćĺ\n  1112Ôćĺ- If the agent requests user input, fail the run attempt immediately.\n  1113Ôćĺ- The client detects this via:\n  1114Ôćĺ  - explicit method (`item/tool/requestUserInput`), or\n  1115Ôćĺ  - turn methods/flags indicating input is required.\n  1116Ôćĺ\n  1117Ôćĺ### 10.6 Timeouts and Error Mapping\n  1118Ôćĺ\n  1119ÔćĺTimeouts:\n  1120Ôćĺ\n  1121Ôćĺ- `codex.read_timeout_ms`: request/response 1124Ôćĺ\n  1125ÔćĺError mapping (recommended normalized categories):\n  1126Ôćĺ\n  1127Ôćĺ- `codex_not_found`\n  1128Ôćĺ- `invalid_workspace_cwd`\n  1129Ôćĺ- `response_timeout`\n  1130Ôćĺ- Contract\n  1138Ôćĺ\n  1139ÔćĺThe `Agent Runner` wraps workspace + prompt + app-server client.\n  1140Ôćĺ\n  1141ÔćĺBehavior:\n  1142Ôćĺ\n  1143Ôćĺ1. Create/reuse workspace for issue.\n  1144Ôćĺ2. Build prompt from workflow template.\n  1145Ôćĺ3. Start app-server session.\n  1146Ôćĺ4. Forward app-server events to orchestrator.\n  1147Ôćĺ5. On any error, fail the worker attempt (the orchestrator will retry).\n  1148Ôćĺ\n  1149ÔćĺNote:\n  1150Ôćĺ\n  1151Ôćĺ- Workspaces are intentionally preserved after successful runs.\n  1152Ôćĺ\n  1153Ôćĺ## 11. Issue Tracker Integration Contract (Linear-Compatible)\n  1154Ôćĺ\n  1155Ôćĺ### 11.1 Required Operations\n  1156Ôćĺ\n  1157ÔćĺAn implementation must support these tracker adapter operations:\n  1158Ôćĺ\n  1159Ôćĺ1. `fetch_candidate_issues()`\n  1160Ôćĺ   - Return issues in configured active states for a configured project.\n  1161Ôćĺ\n  1162Ôćĺ2. `fetch_issues_by_states(state_names)`\n  1163Ôćĺ   - Used for startup terminal cleanup.\n  1164Ôćĺ\n  1165Ôćĺ3. `fetch_issue_states_by_ids(issue_ids)`\n  1166Ôćĺ   - Used for active-run reconciliation.\n  1167Ôćĺ\n  1168Ôćĺ### 11.2 Query Semantics (Linear)\n  1169Ôćĺ\n  1170ÔćĺLinear-specific requirements for `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`:\n  1171Ôćĺ\n  1172Ôćĺ- `tracker.kind == \"linear\"`\n  1173Ôćĺ- GraphQL endpoint (default `https://api.linear.app/graphql`)\n  1174Ôćĺ- Auth token sent in `Authorization` header\n  1175Ôćĺ- `tracker.project_slug` maps to Linear project `slugId`\n  1176Ôćĺ- Candidate issue query filters project using `project: { slugId: { eq: $projectSlug } }`\n  1177Ôćĺ- Issue-state refresh query uses GraphQL issue IDs with variable type `[ID!]`\n  1178Ôćĺ- Pagination required for candidate issues\n  1179Ôćĺ- Page size default: `50`\n  1180Ôćĺ- Network timeout: `30000 ms`\n  1181Ôćĺ\n  1182ÔćĺImportant:\n  1183Ôćĺ\n  1184Ôćĺ- Linear GraphQL schema details can drift. Let me compile the comprehensive report.\n\n---\n\n# How Other Frameworks Enforce Pipeline Step Ordering -- Mechanical Patterns\n\n## The Core Problem\n\nAn AI agent can rationalize skipping any step defined in prose. We need patterns where the system physically prevents step N+1 from executing before step N completes.\n\n---\n\n## 1. CrewAI: Sequential For-Loop + Guardrail Gates\n\n### The Enforcement Mechanism\n\nCrewAI's enforcement is brutally simple: **a Python `for` loop**. There is no way for a task to execute out of order because the execution is controlled by the framework, not by the agent.\n\n**Source**: `lib/crewai/src/crewai/crew.py`, method `_execute_tasks` (line 1180)\n\n```python\ndef _execute_tasks(self, tasks: list[Task], start_index=0, was_replayed=False) -> CrewOutput:\n    task_outputs: list[TaskOutput] = []\n    futures: list[tuple[Task, Future[TaskOutput], int]] = []\n    last_sync_output: TaskOutput | None = None\n\n    for task_index, task in enumerate(tasks):\n        # ... prepare task ...\n        if task.async_execution:\n            future = task.execute_async(agent=exec_data.agent, context=context, tools=exec_data.tools)\n            futures.append((task, future, task_index))\n        else:\n            if futures:\n                task_outputs = self._process_async_tasks(futures, was_replayed)\n                futures.clear()\n            task_output = task.execute_sync(agent=exec_data.agent, context=context, tools=exec_data.tools)\n            task_outputs.append(task_output)\n```\n\nThe agent never decides what to do next. The `for` loop iterates `self.tasks` in declaration order. Each synchronous task **blocks** until it produces a `TaskOutput`. Only then does the loop advance.\n\n### Guardrails as Output Gates\n\n**Source**: `lib/crewai/src/crewai/task.py` (line 1136) and `lib/crewai/src/crewai/utilities/guardrail.py`\n\nThe guardrail is a **post-execution gate** on each task's output. The type signature is:\n\n```python\nGuardrailCallable = Callable[[TaskOutput], tuple[bool, Any]]\n```\n\nThe framework calls the guardrail after the agent finishes. If it returns `(False, error_message)`, the framework:\n1. Feeds the error back to the agent as context\n2. Re-executes the agent on the same task\n3. Retries up to `guardrail_max_retries` (default 3)\n4. If all retries fail, raises an Exception -- halting the pipeline\n\nThe critical insight: **the guardrail is framework-level code, not agent-level code**. The agent cannot bypass it. It runs in the `_invoke_guardrail_function` method at line 1136, and the agent only proceeds to the next task when the guardrail returns `(True, validated_output)`.\n\n### Context Dependencies\n\nThe `Task.context` field (line 143) takes a `list[Task]` -- references to other task objects whose outputs should be injected as context. The `validate_context_no_future_tasks` validator (line 554 of crew.py) physically prevents a task from referencing a future task:\n\n```python\nif task_indices[id(context_task)] > task_indices[id(task)]:\n    raise ValueError(f\"Task '{task.description}' has a context dependency on a future task\")\n```\n\n### ConditionalTask\n\n**Source**: `lib/crewai/src/crewai/tasks/conditional_task.py`\n\nA `ConditionalTask` has a `condition: Callable[[TaskOutput], bool]` that receives the previous task's output. If it returns False, the task is skipped with an empty `TaskOutput`. The condition is **framework code**, not agent code.\n\n### Summary of CrewAI Pattern\n\n| Mechanism | How It Enforces |\n|-----------|----------------|\n| Python `for` loop | Sequential execution is physically a loop iteration |\n| `TaskOutput` return value | Task N must produce output before loop advances |\n| Guardrail function | Post-execution gate; rejects and retries automatically |\n| `context` field + validator | Prevents forward references at construction time |\n| `ConditionalTask.condition` | Framework-level skip decision, not agent decision |\n\n**Key limitation**: CrewAI's ordering is entirely linear (or linear with async bursts). There is no DAG -- it is a flat list.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LangGraph: Channel-Based Dataflow with Barriers\n\n### The Enforcement Mechanism\n\nLangGraph is a **channel-based dataflow engine**. Nodes do not call each other. Instead, each node reads from and writes to named channels. A node is only eligible to execute when its **trigger channels** have been updated since the node last ran.\n\n**Source**: `libs/langgraph/langgraph/pregel/_algo.py`, function `_triggers` (line 1033)\n\n```python\ndef _triggers(channels, versions, seen, null_version, proc) -> bool:\n    if seen is None:\n        for chan in proc.triggers:\n            if channels[chan].is_available():\n                return True\n    else:\n        for chan in proc.triggers:\n            if channels[chan].is_available() and versions.get(chan, null_version) > seen.get(chan, null_version):\n                return True\n    return False\n```\n\nThis is the **mechanical gate**: a node's triggers are channel names. The node can only fire when those channels have new values. If node A writes to channel X, and node B triggers on channel X, then B physically cannot run until A writes to X.\n\n### The Tick Loop\n\n**Source**: `libs/langgraph/langgraph/pregel/_loop.py`, method `tick` (line 461)\n\n```python\ndef tick(self) -> bool:\n    if self.step > self.stop:\n        self.status = \"out_of_steps\"\n        return False\n    \n    self.tasks = prepare_next_tasks(...)  # determines which nodes can fire\n    \n    if not self.tasks:\n        self.status = \"done\"\n        return False\n    \n    if self.interrupt_before and should_interrupt(...):\n        self.status = \"interrupt_before\"\n        raise GraphInterrupt()\n    \n    return True  # execute the prepared tasks\n```\n\nThe execution engine calls `prepare_next_tasks` which iterates candidate nodes and checks `_triggers`. Only nodes whose channels are ready get scheduled. This is not a suggestion -- it is a physical impossibility for a node to run if its input channels are empty.\n\n### NamedBarrierValue: Multi-Edge Wait\n\n**Source**: `libs/langgraph/langgraph/channels/named_barrier_value.py`\n\nWhen you call `add_edge([A, B, C], D)` -- meaning D waits for A, B, and C -- LangGraph creates a `NamedBarrierValue` channel:\n\n```python\nclass NamedBarrierValue(BaseChannel):\n    def __init__(self, typ, names: set):\n        self.names = names  # e.g. {\"A\", \"B\", \"C\"}\n        self.seen = set()\n    \n    def update(self, values):\n        for value in values:\n            if value in self.names:\n                self.seen.add(value)\n    \n    def is_available(self) -> bool:\n        return self.seen == self.names  # only available when ALL names are seen\n    \n    def consume(self) -> bool:\n        if self.seen == self.names:\n            self.seen = set()\n            return True\n        return False\n```\n\nNode D triggers on this barrier channel. The barrier is only \"available\" (returns True from `is_available()`) when every named predecessor has written to it. This is a **join gate** -- it enforces fan-in ordering mechanically.\n\n### interrupt() as Execution Pause\n\n**Source**: `libs/langgraph/langgraph/types.py`, function `interrupt` (line 705)\n\n```python\ndef interrupt(value: Any) -> Any:\n    conf = get_config()[\"configurable\"]\n    scratchpad = conf[CONFIG_KEY_SCRATCHPAD]\n    idx = scratchpad.interrupt_counter()\n    \n    # Check for previously saved resume values\n    if scratchpad.resume:\n        if idx < len(scratchpad.resume):\n            return scratchpad.resume[idx]\n    \n    # No resume value -- raise exception to halt\n    raise GraphInterrupt(\n        (Interrupt.from_ns(value=value, ns=conf[CONFIG_KEY_CHECKPOINT_NS]),)\n    )\n```\n\n`interrupt()` physically raises `GraphInterrupt`, which halts the node. The graph state is checkpointed. To resume, a client must send `Command(resume=value)`. The graph replays from the start of the node, and this time `interrupt()` returns the resume value instead of raising.\n\nThis requires a **checkpointer** (persistent storage). Without it, `interrupt()` cannot work -- the state would be lost.\n\n### Conditional Edges\n\n`add_conditional_edges(source, path_fn, path_map)` lets a function decide the next node. But it is framework-level code -- the path function runs in the engine, not in the agent. The agent cannot override the routing.\n\n### Summary of LangGraph Pattern\n\n| Mechanism | How It Enforces |\n|-----------|----------------|\n| Channel triggers | Node only fires when input channels have new data |\n| `_triggers` version check | Compares channel versions against node's \"last seen\" |\n| NamedBarrierValue | Multi-predecessor join gate -- all must complete |\n| `prepare_next_tasks` | Engine determines eligible tasks each step |\n| `interrupt()` + GraphInterrupt | Physically halts execution via exception |\n| Checkpoint persistence | State survives pause/resume across process boundaries |\n\n**Key strength**: True DAG execution with fan-in/fan-out. The agent writes state updates; the framework decides what runs next.\n\n---\n\n## 3. GitHub Actions `needs:` -- DAG Scheduling\n\n### The Enforcement Mechanism\n\nGitHub Actions uses a **DAG scheduler** where jobs declare their dependencies via the `needs:` keyword. The scheduler physically will not start a job until all its `needs:` jobs have completed successfully.\n\nThe mechanism works as follows:\n\n1. **Job dependency graph**: At workflow parse time, the `needs:` declarations are assembled into a DAG. Circular dependencies are rejected.\n2. **State machine per job**: Each job has states: `queued`, `in_progress`, `completed`, `failed`, `skipped`. A job transitions from `queued` to `in_progress` only when all jobs in its `needs:` list are in `completed` state.\n3. **Failure propagation**: If a needed job fails, the dependent job is skipped (unless `if: always()` is used). This is a hard gate.\n4. **Output passing**: A job can consume outputs from its `needs:` jobs via `needs.<job_id>.outputs.<output_name>`. These outputs are only available after the needed job completes.\n\n```yaml\njobs:\n  build:\n    runs-on: ubuntu-latest\n    outputs:\n      artifact-path: ${{ steps.build.outputs.path }}\n    steps: [...]\n  \n  test:\n    needs: build       # physically cannot start until build completes\n    runs-on: ubuntu-latest\n    steps: [...]\n  \n  deploy:\n    needs: [build, test]  # fan-in: waits for BOTH\n    steps: [...]\n```\n\n### The Pattern\n\n- **Declaration**: Dependencies are declared in data (YAML), not in code\n- **Enforcement**: The scheduler is the sole authority -- jobs cannot start themselves\n- **Artifact gating**: Outputs from needed jobs are the data bridge between steps\n- **Failure = skip**: A failed dependency cascades as skip, not as \"try anyway\"\n\n---\n\n## 4. Temporal.io: Deterministic Replay + Await Blocking\n\n### The Enforcement Mechanism\n\nTemporal enforces ordering through **deterministic workflow code** combined with **language-level await**. Activities (side effects) are async operations that the workflow awaits:\n\n**Source**: `temporalio/workflow.py`, line 2630\n\n```python\nasync def execute_activity(activity, arg=..., **kwargs) -> Any:\n    \"\"\"Start an activity and wait for completion.\n    This is a shortcut for `await` start_activity().\n    \"\"\"\n    return await _Runtime.current().workflow_start_activity(activity, *args, **kwargs)\n```\n\n`execute_activity` is an `async` function that returns an `ActivityHandle`, which extends `asyncio.Task`. When you write:\n\n```python\n@workflow.defn\nclass MyWorkflow:\n    @workflow.run\n    async def run(self):\n        result_a = await workflow.execute_activity(step_a, ...)\n        result_b = await workflow.execute_activity(step_b, result_a, ...)\n        result_c = await workflow.execute_activity(step_c, result_b, ...)\n```\n\nThe `await` keyword is the enforcement mechanism. `step_b` literally cannot execute until `step_a`'s `ActivityHandle` resolves. This is not a convention -- it is a language-level guarantee from Python's async/await.\n\n### Event Sourcing and Replay\n\nTemporal's deeper enforcement comes from its **event sourcing** model:\n\n1. The workflow function runs in a **deterministic sandbox** -- no random I/O, no wall-clock time\n2. Every activity completion is recorded as an **event** in Temporal's event history\n3. On replay (crash recovery), the workflow re-executes from the beginning, but `execute_activity` calls return the previously recorded result instead of re-executing\n4. If the workflow code tries to run activities in a different order than the recorded history, Temporal throws a **non-determinism error** and halts\n\nThis means:\n- Step ordering is enforced by `await` at write time\n- Step ordering is **verified** by replay at recovery time\n- You physically cannot change the order of steps after they have been recorded\n\n### Parallel Fan-Out / Fan-In\n\nFor parallel activities, you use `start_activity` (non-blocking) followed by `await`:\n\n```python\nhandle_a = workflow.start_activity(step_a, ...)\nhandle_b = workflow.start_activity(step_b, ...)\nresult_a = await handle_a\nresult_b = await handle_b\nresult_c = await workflow.execute_activity(step_c, result_a, result_b, ...)\n```\n\n`step_c` physically cannot run until both handles resolve.\n\n### Summary of Temporal Pattern\n\n| Mechanism | How It Enforces |\n|-----------|----------------|\n| `await execute_activity()` | Language-level blocking -- next line cannot run |\n| Event sourcing | Records activity completion as immutable history |\n| Deterministic replay | Verifies ordering on crash recovery |\n| Non-determinism detection | Halts if replay order differs from history |\n| `ActivityHandle` (asyncio.Task) | Activity result is a future that must be awaited |\n\n---\n\n## 5. OpenAI Symphony: State Machine + Lifecycle Phases\n\n### The Enforcement Mechanism\n\n**Source**: `SPEC.md` from `github.com/openai/symphony`\n\nSymphony uses a **two-level state machine** for ordering enforcement:\n\n**Level 1: Issue Orchestration States** (Section 7.1)\n```\nUnclaimed -> Claimed -> Running -> Released\n                    -> RetryQueued -> (re-dispatch or Released)\n```\n\n**Level 2: Run Attempt Lifecycle** (Section 7.2)\n```\nPreparingWorkspace -> BuildingPrompt -> LaunchingAgentProcess -> InitializingSession \n  -> StreamingTurn -> Finishing -> Succeeded | Failed | TimedOut | Stalled | CanceledByReconciliation\n```\n\nThese are **strict sequential phases**. The code physically cannot launch the agent process before the workspace is prepared, because the workspace path is an input to the launch step.\n\n### Tick-Based Orchestration (Section 8.1)\n\nEach poll tick follows a fixed sequence:\n1. Reconcile running issues\n2. Run dispatch preflight validation\n3. Fetch candidate issues\n4. Sort by priority\n5. Dispatch eligible issues\n\nThis is enforced by a linear function -- steps 3-5 cannot run if step 2 (validation) fails. Validation failure skips dispatch for that tick but keeps reconciliation active.\n\n### Dispatch Eligibility Gates (Section 8.2)\n\nAn issue can only be dispatched if ALL of these are true:\n- Has required fields (id, identifier, title, state)\n- State is in `active_states` and not in `terminal_states`\n- Not already in `running` map\n- Not already in `claimed` set\n- Global concurrency slots available\n- Per-state concurrency slots available\n- Blocker rule passes (no non-terminal blockers for Todo state)\n\nThese are **data-level guards** -- the orchestrator checks hard conditions before allowing dispatch. The coding agent cannot override these checks.\n\n### Session Startup Handshake (Section 10.2)\n\nThe agent runner enforces a strict message ordering protocol:\n1. `initialize` request (wait for response)\n2. `initialized` notification\n3. `thread/start` request\n4. `turn/start` request\n\nEach step depends on data from the previous step (thread_id from step 3 is needed for step 4). This is structural enforcement -- you cannot skip step 3 because step 4 needs `threadId`.\n\n### Summary of Symphony Pattern\n\n| Mechanism | How It Enforces |\n|-----------|----------------|\n| Two-level state machine | Phase transitions are coded, not prompted |\n| Tick sequence | Fixed function order; validation gates dispatch |\n| Eligibility checks | Hard boolean conditions before dispatch |\n| Data dependencies | Each phase produces data the next phase requires |\n| Protocol handshake | Message ordering enforced by response dependencies |\n\n---\n\n## 6. The Universal Pattern\n\nAcross all five frameworks, the same three-layer pattern emerges:\n\n### Layer 1: Control Inversion (Who Decides What Runs Next)\n\n**The agent never decides what step to run next. The framework does.**\n\n- CrewAI: Python `for` loop iterates the task list\n- LangGraph: `prepare_next_tasks` checks channel readiness\n- GitHub Actions: DAG scheduler evaluates `needs:`\n- Temporal: `await` blocks at the language level\n- Symphony: Orchestrator tick sequence is a fixed function\n\nThis is the most important insight: **the framework holds the program counter, not the agent**. The agent executes within a step; it does not choose the step.\n\n### Layer 2: Artifact Gates (What Must Exist Before the Next Step)\n\n**Step N produces a concrete artifact that step N+1 physically requires as input.**\n\n- CrewAI: `TaskOutput` object is passed as `context` to next task\n- LangGraph: Channel values -- nodes read from channels that predecessors write to\n- GitHub Actions: `needs.<job>.outputs` -- outputs are only available after completion\n- Temporal: The `await` return value -- the activity result is the input to the next line\n- Symphony: Workspace path, thread_id, turn_id -- each phase produces data the next needs\n\nThis is stronger than \"check that step N is marked complete.\" It means step N+1 cannot even formulate its request without the output of step N.\n\n### Layer 3: Rejection + Retry (What Happens When a Step's Output Is Invalid)\n\n**A validation gate after each step can reject the output and force retry.**\n\n- CrewAI: Guardrail function returns `(False, error)` -> agent re-executes with error context\n- LangGraph: `interrupt()` raises GraphInterrupt -> execution pauses until human provides input\n- GitHub Actions: Job failure -> dependent jobs skip (or retry with `if: always()`)\n- Temporal: Activity failure -> retry policy with exponential backoff\n- Symphony: Dispatch preflight validation -> skips dispatch on failure, retries on next tick\n\n### The Minimum Implementation\n\nFor Claude Code agent pipeline enforcement, the minimum viable pattern is:\n\n```\nÔöîÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÉ\nÔöé                 FRAMEWORK LAYER                      Ôöé\nÔöé  (holds the program counter, not the agent)          Ôöé\nÔöé                                                      Ôöé\nÔöé  for phase in pipeline:                              Ôöé\nÔöé      1. Check preconditions (artifact from prev)     Ôöé\nÔöé      2. Execute agent within phase boundary           Ôöé\nÔöé      3. Validate output (guardrail gate)              Ôöé\nÔöé      4. Persist artifact to state store               Ôöé\nÔöé      5. Only then: advance to next phase              Ôöé\nÔöé                                                      Ôöé\nÔöé  The agent sees: \"You are in phase X. Here is the    Ôöé\nÔöé  output from phase X-1. Produce artifact Y.\"         Ôöé\nÔöé  The agent does NOT see: \"Here is the full pipeline, Ôöé\nÔöé  decide what to do.\"                                 Ôöé\nÔööÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöÇÔöś\n```\n\nThe three mechanical requirements:\n\n1. **Control inversion**: The framework iterates phases. The agent is called within a phase, not given the phase list to self-navigate.\n\n2. **Artifact dependency**: Phase N+1 requires a typed artifact from phase N. Not \"check if phase N ran\" -- literally \"pass phase N's output as phase N+1's input.\" If the artifact doesn't exist, the function call fails at the language level.\n\n3. **Output validation**: A guardrail function (framework code, not agent code) inspects each phase's output before the artifact is persisted. Rejection triggers retry with error feedback, up to a max retry count.\n\n### What This Means for Wazir\n\nThe current Wazir pipeline likely describes phases in a prompt or configuration that the agent reads and follows. The agent can rationalize skipping. To make it mechanical:\n\n1. **The workflow runner should hold the loop**, not the agent. Each phase is a separate agent invocation, not a section of a long-running conversation.\n\n2. **Phase outputs should be typed artifacts** stored in the state DB (SQLite). Phase N+1's agent invocation should receive phase N's artifact as structured input, not as \"go read what you did before.\"\n\n3. **Guardrails should be code functions** (in hooks or skill validators), not prompt instructions. A guardrail that checks \"does the plan contain at least 3 items?\" is a Python function returning `(bool, str)`, not a line in the system prompt.\n\n4. **The agent should never see the full pipeline**. It should see only: \"You are executing phase: {name}. Your input is: {previous_artifact}. Produce: {expected_output_schema}.\"\n\nThis is the pattern that works everywhere: **give the agent a task, not a plan**."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":570,"cache_read_input_tokens":96630,"output_tokens":5491,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":570},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZEQFJwfixFPmxvYUyJY2","type":"assistant","uuid":"b78ee631-f3d3-487d-ace8-e199575880ca","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:23:16.636Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}
